         <div class="author-comment">
          <cite class="fn">
           <a class="url" href="http://www.gauravonomics.com/blog/top-experts-share-their-best-kept-marketing-secrets/" rel="external nofollow">
            Gauravonomics
           </a>
          </cite>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://smallbiztrends.com/2008/01/top-experts-dish-with-their-best-kept-marketing-secrets.html#comment-480100">
            February 16, 2008 at 12:11 am
           </a>
          </div>
          <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
         </div>
         <div class="clear">
         </div>
         <div class="comment-content">
          <p>
           Heres my own best kept marketing secret  learn how to give the perfect elevator pitch.
          </p>
          <p>
           An elevator pitch is an overview of an idea for a product, service, or project that can be delivered in the time span of an elevator ride (say, thirty seconds or 100-150 words). Knowing how to make the perfect elevator pitch is important because sometimes thirty seconds is all you get with your boss, client or investor.
          </p>
          <p>
           I use a simple three step template to make my own elevator pitches 
          </p>
          <p>
            Step 1  Describe your idea in one or two sentences. Give both facts as they are and your own opinions.
          </p>
          <p>
            Step 2  Specify what exactly you want to be done, by when and by whom.
          </p>
          <p>
            Step 3  Give three reasons why, including examples to illustrate the benefits.
          </p>
          <p>
           Now that you know how to make the perfect elevator pitch, why dont you make one today?
          </p>
          <p>
           By the way, head your to my blog to read &lt;a href=http://www.gauravonomics.com/blog/top-experts-share-their-best-kept-marketing-secrets/&gt;the perfect elevator pitch for the Best Kept Marketing Secrets e-book&lt;/a&gt;.
          </p>
         </div>

         <div class="comment-content">
          <p>
           My favorite post in quite some time. Thank you for all the great tips and insights.
          </p>
          <p>
           Top secret:
          </p>
          <p>
           Your brand should permeate your company, through and through.  Customers are empowered to engage companies through more diverse channels and touch points than ever before.  However, its still more common to put the typical marketing &amp; communication tactics (advertising, website, etc.) against brand screen rigor while other company tools can feel like an afterthought (i.e. answering the phone/customer service, sales materials, store/office layout, even your email signature and business cards).
          </p>
          <p>
           Every single customer touch point is an opportunity to make a brand impression.  One touch point may be the only impression you get, so while it makes sense to prioritize your marketing focus, dont discount your brand elsewhere.   Fully integrated marketing plans are key in creating a meaningful and memorable customer experience.  And it doesnt have to mean spending more  just thinking more.
          </p>
          <p>
           Mike Covert
           <br/>
           Partner  Ignite Studios
           <br/>
           Dallas, TX
          </p>

          <p>
           The best secret? Ive got some:
           <br/>
            Remember, You become more vulnerable when everyone else is talking about how good you are.
           <br/>
            Competitor is not just that who sells similar products/services but all those whom your clients have interactivity because your customer services will be compared.
           <br/>
            Attention to details.
           <br/>
            Every time your client is contacted an opportunity to create value is given.
           <br/>
            Make easy for client express themselves
           <br/>
            Quality is more than limited possibility. quality is about unlimited possiblities
           <br/>
            Always carry two business cards. One with your details and another one in blank, so if you meet someone with no cards, you can offer it to him/her fill up and give back to you.
           <br/>
            Call everyone by their name.
           <br/>
            Best ads come from attempts to solve problems
           <br/>
            A good advertisement is one which sells the product without drawing attention to itself (from Ogilvy!)
          </p>
          <p>
           Thats all
           <br/>
           Lucio Dias Ribeiro

       <li id="comment-482552">
        <div class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 comment-wrap">
         <div class="comment-avatar">
          <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-45 photo" height="45" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/614929b6beae49b6b703a8f66ec44714?s=45&amp;d=mm&amp;r=pg" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/614929b6beae49b6b703a8f66ec44714?s=90&amp;d=mm&amp;r=pg 2x" width="45"/>
         </div>
         <div class="author-comment">
          <cite class="fn">
           <a class="url" href="http://elevatingyourbusiness.com" rel="external nofollow">
            Maria Marsala
           </a>
          </cite>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://smallbiztrends.com/2008/01/top-experts-dish-with-their-best-kept-marketing-secrets.html#comment-482552">
            February 18, 2008 at 12:58 pm
           </a>
          </div>
          <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
         </div>
         <div class="clear">
         </div>
         <div class="comment-content">
          <p>
           Create an ideal client and marketing to your target.  See if youre doing that now.
          </p>
          <p>
           Is Your Business Targeting Your Ideal Client?
          </p>
          <p>
           Small to mid-size business owners, branch office managers, and independent agents, rate your clients against your ideal, and see if its time to make a change OR if youre on the mark.
          </p>
          <p>
           Rating System     1 = Disaster     3= Average     5 = Brilliantly Successful
          </p>
          <p>
           1.	_______My business has a solution to a problem that my IC wants to fix now.
           <br/>
           2.	_______My ideal client is the decision maker.
           <br/>
           3.	_______There are at least 2 local organizations where 75% of the members are my IC.
           <br/>
           4.	_______On the whole, my IC can easily afford my services and wants to pay my rates.
           <br/>
           5.	_______My IC clearly sees me as unique and more qualified than others offering
           <br/>
           similar services.
           <br/>
           6.	_______My clients refer people to me all the time; I dont have to ask.
           <br/>
           7.	_______When I market, network, or advertise, I always end up with solid leads.
           <br/>
           8.	_______I do not have to educate my IC about the value of what I do.
           <br/>
           9.	_______I know everything about my ideal client  from their attitude, to shopping patterns,  to
           <br/>
           what they read, to what makes them tick.
           <br/>
           10.	_______When I network or speak, 85% of the time is spent in front my IC or people who know
           <br/>
           them very well.
           <br/>
           11.	_______I spend very little time explaining what I do to my IC, because they already get it.
           <br/>
           12.	_______I love working with my ideal client who keeps their word close to 100% of the time.
           <br/>
           13.	_______My ideal client has the financial means to invest in the solutions they need.
           <br/>
           14.	_______There are others, that I can form alliances with that are selling to my ideal client.
          </p>
          <p>
           Scoring:  Congratulations! Youve now assessed how well youre attracting your IC to your business. Since you must consider all the above in your successful business/unit, its not the total number that counts; its how well you do in each area!
          </p>
          <p>
           However, a number of 1s and 3s is a definite signal for improvement. If youre ready to grow your business to the next level, or further define your Ideal Clientto truly change the state of your business in the next twelve monthsits time to visit
           <a href="http://www.CorporateSecretsForSmallBusinessSuccess.com" rel="nofollow">
            http://www.CorporateSecretsForSmallBusinessSuccess.com
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           (c) 2008 Maria Marsala, Elevating Your Business
          </p>

         <div class="comment-content">
          <p>
           As they say  keep your friends close and your enemies closer. In a marketing context, it is essential to know all about your key competitors as the information you get, will allow you to take advantage of their weaknesses and defend against their strengths.
          </p>
          <p>
           By analyzing your competitors it helps you to work out your key point of difference and what you do better. Sources of information to find out more about your competitors include their website, trade associations, internet search engines, your customers and dont forget to buy their product to experience their customer service.
          </p>
          <p>
           Remember they would probably love to have some of your customers for their business and they are probably keeping a close watch on you,
          </p>
          <p>
           Susan
           <br/>
           M4B Marketing Software

          <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->

         <div class="clear">

         <div class="comment-content">
          <p>
           My best kept marketing secret is to ask three customer centric questions:
          </p>
          <p>
           1. Step into the role of your customers and ask yourself: Would you buy your product, honestly?
           <br/>
           The answers will help you better understand why people buy and why they dont buy.
          </p>
          <p>
           2. Do you use your own product?
           <br/>
           It always amazes me how many companies find lots of excuses of not using their own products  probably the same reasons why their customers dont.
          </p>
          <p>
           3. Are you selling a product, or are you selling the value (of the product)?
           <br/>
           People dont buy products; they buy the VALUE of the product. Dont market and sell features, sell the value of the features.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a href="http://www.startupramp.com" rel="nofollow">
            http://www.startupramp.com
           </a>
          </p>

           <br/>
           3. Act (Now that youve actually listed, DO SOMETHING about it, act!)
           <br/>
           4. Ask again (Now its time to measure your success and do it all again.)

       <!-- #comment-## -->
       <li id="comment-687945">
        <div class="comment even thread-even depth-1 comment-wrap">
         <div class="comment-avatar">
          <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-45 photo" height="45" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e2376f22b93fb12b604e0ca18711e8f9?s=45&amp;d=mm&amp;r=pg" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e2376f22b93fb12b604e0ca18711e8f9?s=90&amp;d=mm&amp;r=pg 2x" width="45"/>
         </div>
         <div class="author-comment">
          <cite class="fn">
           <a class="url" href="http://www.computerforensicsassociates.com" rel="external nofollow">
            donna
           </a>
          </cite>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://smallbiztrends.com/2008/01/top-experts-dish-with-their-best-kept-marketing-secrets.html#comment-687945">
            December 16, 2009 at 2:59 pm
           </a>
          </div>
          <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
         </div>
         <div class="clear">
         </div>
         <div class="comment-content">
          <p>
           Listen!  To your customer.  Ascertain what they really need.
           <br/>
           CARE!  Care about them, their problems, their issues, their dog!  We live in a very cold world, caring about your customer (really caring) will set you apart automatically.
           <br/>
           Deliver!  Setup yourself up towards integrity.  People respect honestyif you cant deliver what the customer wants.say so. Upfront and then explain to the customer what you can do.
           <br/>
           Do NOT lie!  Bait &amp; Switch, exaggerate your services.  How can you really care about your customer if you can lie about your products/services.  Impossible.  Yet I see this all the time.  Dont do it.
          </p>
          <p>
           Be yourself, listen to your customers needs, care about them then deliver what you said you would give them and make certain that what you deliver is what they were expecting to purchase.  Sounds simple, but many do not do this.
          </p>
         </div>
         <div class="reply">
          <a aria-label="Reply to donna" class="comment-reply-link" href="/2008/01/top-experts-dish-with-their-best-kept-marketing-secrets.html?replytocom=687945#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-687945", "687945", "respond", "1664" )'>
           Reply
          </a>
         </div>

				$(".user_votes").children().not(":input").hide();
				// Create stars for: Average rating

					inputType: "select",
					cancelShow: true,
					captionEl: $(".caption"),
					callback: function(ui, type, value) {

						// Send request to the server using POST method
					$.post("http://smallbiztrends.com/wp-admin/admin-ajax.php", { action: 'sr_save_vote', post_id: 1664, rate: value }, function(response) {
						// Select stars from "Average rating" control to match the returned average rating value
						$(".avg").stars("select", Math.round(response.avg));
						// Update other text controls...
						$(".all_votes-1664").text(response.votes);
						$(".all_avg1664").text(response.avg);
						// Display confirmation message to the user
						$(".messages").text("Rating saved (" + value + "). Thanks!").stop().css("opacity", 1).fadeIn(30);
						// Hide confirmation message and enable stars for "Rate this" control, after 2 sec...
						setTimeout(function(){
							$(".messages").fadeOut(1000, function(){})
						}, 2000);
					}, "json" );
				}
			});
			// Since the &lt;option value="3"&gt; was selected by default, we must remove selection from Stars.
			//$(".rat").stars("selectID", -1);
			// Create element to use for confirmation messages
			$('&lt;div class="messages"/&gt;').appendTo(".rat");
		});
		//]]&gt;
  </script>
